The City's Climate Turns Cold; Epidemics Still Rampant 145

Sixty-six Deaths from Infectious Diseases Last Week

Typhoid fever, pulmonary tuberculosis, and diphtheria are most common.

According to reports from the Seaport Quarantine Station, the Public Concession Health Department, and the French Concession Health Department, the number of infectious disease cases last week included: smallpox 6 cases; scarlet fever 24 cases; cerebrospinal meningitis 5 cases, 2 deaths; typhoid fever and paratyphoid fever 56 cases; dysentery 38 cases, 4 deaths; diphtheria 43 cases, 7 deaths; influenza 3 cases; pulmonary tuberculosis and pneumonia 26 cases, 18 deaths; beriberi 1 case, 1 death; measles 2 cases, 1 death; malaria 11 cases, 2 deaths; schistosomiasis 1 case; chickenpox 1 case. The total number of cases was 217, with a total of 66 deaths. Typhoid fever and severe typhoid fever were the most common causes of death, followed by pulmonary tuberculosis, pneumonia, diphtheria, and dysentery.

Perpetrator of the Xuan Sheng Assassination Case Indicted; Trial Expected Soon in the District Court 146

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau solved the Xuan Sheng assassination case. The perpetrators Wang Zhensheng, Mao Yonghu, Zhao Yunhong, Jin Daozhen, and related women Wang Zai and Zhang Mo, totaling six individuals, were found to be involved. The investigation revealed that the accused were instigated by Hua Ke, a cadre of the reactionary faction, to disrupt order and cause international disputes. They confessed and were transferred to the District Court Procuratorate. After repeated investigations and clear evidence, the prosecutor has indicted the accused on charges of murder. After the entire case file was transferred to the criminal court, the trial is expected to open soon. However, the accused are in custody, and their families, fearing implication, have not visited them in jail. Therefore, defense lawyers have not been hired. The court will appoint public defenders to represent them in the future.

Minsheng Company's Minyu Vessel Grounded En Route from Yichang to Chongqing; Minsheng, Minzhi, Minxuan, and Minting Vessels Dispatched for Rescue; Passengers and Cargo Transferred to Minzhi Vessel, Which Arrived in Chongqing Yesterday 147

The Minsheng Industrial Company's Minyu vessel, which runs on the Yichang-Chongqing route, grounded while carrying cargo and passengers from Yichang to Chongqing on the morning of the 15th of this month in the Shijiahe section of the Yangtze River near Changshou. The company dispatched four vessels, Minsheng, Minzhi, Minxuan, and Minting, for rescue. Details are as follows:

Accidental Grounding

The Minyu vessel has a gross tonnage of 232 tons and a net tonnage of 119 tons. It usually travels on the Chongqing-Fuling-Wanxian route. Due to the current dry season on the Sichuan River, it switched to the Yichang-Chongqing route. On November 13th, it transferred cargo and passengers from the Shanghai-Yichang Qianminquan vessel in Yichang and set sail for Chongqing. On the morning of the 15th, it ran aground on a reef in the Shijiahe section of the Yangtze River near Changshou. As a result, the bottom of the ship was breached by the reef, and river water flooded in. The captain tried to rescue the vessel, but his efforts were unsuccessful.

Four Vessels for Rescue

The captain immediately put on full speed and steered the vessel to a sandy beach to prevent it from sinking. At the same time, he telegraphed the company to dispatch vessels for rescue. Upon receiving the report, the Chongqing General Company immediately dispatched four vessels: the Minsheng vessel with a gross tonnage of 71 tons, the Minzhi vessel with a gross tonnage of 216 tons, the Minxuan vessel with a gross tonnage of 153 tons, and the Minting vessel with a gross tonnage of 64 tons, to the scene of the accident for rescue.

Passengers Arrive in Chongqing

The Minsheng, Minzhi, Minxuan, and Minting vessels have all arrived at the scene of the Minyu accident. All passengers were transferred to the Minzhi vessel, and the cargo was also transferred to the Minzhi vessel for transport to Chongqing. Fortunately, the dozens of passengers were all unharmed. However, some of the cargo in the hold had been damaged by water. The Minzhi vessel safely arrived in Chongqing yesterday.

Efforts to Tow Back

As for the grounded Minyu vessel, the Minxuan, Minting, and Minsheng vessels are making efforts to tow it back. The breached area is being sealed with cement, and the water that flooded in is being pumped out. The vessel is currently still grounded on the sandy beach. After the water level rises, further efforts will be made to tow it back to Chongqing for repairs in the shipyard. It is reported that the losses are considerable.

Animal Protection Society Requests Strict Prohibition of Slaughtering Pregnant Sheep and Live Deer for Antlers to Curb Cruelty and Maintain Animal Husbandry 148

The China Animal Protection Society, based on a letter from Gao Depei, an animal husbandry instructor in Fengxian County, requesting that the authorities strictly prohibit the cruel slaughter of pregnant sheep, and based on a letter from member Zhu Guixin requesting a ban on slaughtering deer for antlers, submitted letters to the relevant authorities yesterday, requesting prompt action to stop the practice, curb cruelty, and preserve animal husbandry. The original text is as follows:

Strictly Prohibit the Cruel Slaughter of Pregnant Sheep

Ye Gongchuo, Chairman of the Society, and Guan Jiongzhi, Vice Chairman, submitted a letter to both the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry, stating: "We are submitting this report based on information received. According to a letter from Gao Depei, an animal husbandry instructor at the Fengxian County Agricultural Extension Office, foreign merchants have recently been buying pregnant ewes in the northern part of our country, luring farmers to strip the skin from the unborn lambs. As a result, in recent years, there have been tens of thousands of brokers trading in this type of raw skin in the areas north of the Yangtze River and in Shandong Province. This has led to a significant decrease in the number of sheep in the Jiangbei region in the past two years. Taking Fengxian County as an example, the number of sheep three years ago was 210,000, but in recent years, there have only been 40,000 to 50,000. If this continues, the breed of sheep will be extinct in the future. Farmers' cruel slaughter of pregnant ewes is inhumane and should be prohibited by law. It also hinders the current promotion of animal husbandry and breed improvement. Depei's duty is to report to the relevant industry and construction authorities for verification. We are also sending this letter to your society, with the aim of protecting animals, to request the central government to issue a strict ban. This will greatly benefit the future of animal husbandry in China." The cruel slaughter of pregnant sheep is extremely inhumane, killing two lives with one act, and is against human ethics. Such destruction not only hinders the future of animal husbandry but also threatens the extinction of sheep. Therefore, we submit this report to the authorities for review, requesting that you promptly issue a notice to all provinces to strictly prohibit this practice, to protect animal life and promote benevolence, which would be greatly appreciated.

Prohibit Slaughtering Deer for Antlers

Ye and Guan, the two chairmen of the society, sent a letter to the Nantong County government yesterday, requesting a ban on slaughtering deer for antlers. The letter stated: "According to a letter from Zhu Guisheng, the Suisheng Pharmacy outside the South Gate of your jurisdiction has scheduled the slaughter of deer for antlers on November 18th, and has widely advertised this event. These innocent animals will suffer a tragic slaughter. Please take action to rescue them." The deer antlers sold by pharmacies are cut from live deer. Not only is the sight of animals trembling and dying unbearable for benevolent people, but the surrounding onlookers can also easily cause cruel practices, which are against human ethics. We are sending this letter to your county government for investigation and prevention, to curb cruelty and rectify people's hearts. We also hope that you will investigate and reply.

Failed Speculation: A Couple Commits Suicide by Poison; Wife Dies, Husband in Critical Condition; Family Tragedy; Aging Parents in Unbearable Grief 149

Chu Xiangfu, a local resident of No. 5 Shanqing Lane, Ninghe, in the city, is 70 years old. His wife, Sun, is 63 years old. They have only one son, Chu Junsheng, who is 30 years old. He is both the heir to the family line and a adopted son, and a promising young man. He works at a gold exchange. Because he is filial to his parents and trustworthy, he is not yet married at the age of 30. He believes that he must be self-sufficient and have money before getting married. So, he did not marry until March 20th of this year, when he married a Miss Yao from Tangjia Lane. She is 20 years old and has good qualities. The family was harmonious and happy, and the two elders were always smiling. Who would have thought that starting this year, all industries would be depressed? He had to resort to speculation and was heavily indebted by Yu Chao in Lan. Chu Junsheng, a conservative and decent man, did not tell his parents about this. As his debts piled up and life became difficult, he had the idea of suicide for a long time, and his beloved wife in the boudoir agreed to die with him. However, they did not reveal their plans, fearing to hurt the elders. A few days ago, he once told his mother that he wanted to travel to Nanjing. His mother stopped him because the weather was bad and the journey would be difficult. Unexpectedly, the young couple went out together the day before yesterday and returned late. His mother asked them about their dinner. Junsheng said that they had eaten at his wife's family. They slept until 7:30 AM yesterday. His mother saw that her son and daughter-in-law had not gotten up yet. Because they always got up at 7:00 AM to wash, dress, and have breakfast before going out, she told the maid to check on them. She heard groaning and was frightened to report to her mistress. Sun opened the door and saw that her daughter-in-law was dead, and her son was foaming at the mouth and groaning incessantly. She immediately sent her son to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. He was diagnosed with suicide by poison, but he was in a coma and still in critical condition. As for the dead daughter-in-law, the police station ordered the local security guard Zhu Shunqing to report to the District Court. Inspector Lei was commissioned to examine the body. The Chu elders were in tears all day, grieving beyond words. It is a truly tragic event.

Moore Memorial Church on Thachin Road in this city, in order to promote the truth of the cross, has scheduled public lectures on "The Wonderful Cross," "The Victorious Cross," and "The Glorious Cross" in the church's main hall at 5:30 PM to 6:30 PM on the afternoons of the 16th, 17th, and 18th. The lectures will be given by Pastor Jiang Changchuan each day. A rotating neon cross will be erected on the top of the church's seven-story bell tower, and will be lit on the 18th. It weighs over 2,200 pounds and was manufactured in the United States. A year ago, when Mr. Shi Huide from Stockton, California, USA, came to Shanghai, he was deeply moved by the church's work and donated the cross. There are still two lectures to be given today and tomorrow. Members of the public are welcome to attend.

Female Dancer from Sanle Dance Company Swindled After Responding to Advertisement at Hotel; Mr. Zhang Forcibly Borrowed Gold Ring and Refused to Return It; Teahouse Worker Wang Yongchen is an Accomplice; Another Female Dancer Previously Swindled 153

At 1:40 PM the day before yesterday, the Sanle Dance Company at No. 18 Ren'an Lane, Guling Road, suddenly received a phone call from a Mr. Zhang, ordering them to send a female dancer to room 37 of the Card Hotel at No. 8 Lane 143, Carter Road. There was a Man in the Room

Who claimed to be the Mr. Zhang who had called. After a considerable amount of time, around 4:00 PM, Mr. Zhang ordered Zhang Xiuying to sleep with him. Zhang refused and shouted loudly, but Wang Yongchen turned a deaf ear and did not enter the room to intervene. Seeing that Zhang Xiuying was wearing a gold ring worth about 20 yuan, the man had bad intentions. He asked to

To look at the style, and took it off her finger and put it on his own finger. Zhang asked for it back, but he refused to return it, leading to another dispute. At that time, Wang Yongchen entered the room and said to Zhang Xiuying, "Mr. Zhang is a young master and would not be surprised even by a diamond ring. Why bother about a mere gold ring?" Zhang had not Returned.

So she immediately called the company to report what had happened. Suspected Wang

And searched him, finding a gold ring in Wang's pocket. Zhang Xiuying recognized the ring as belonging to dancer No. 2, Song Lijun from Ningbo, at the same company. The detective then summoned Song. Li Guojie Case: The Court Summoned Again Yesterday; Li Has Submitted a Petition to the Premier of the Executive Yuan Requesting Pardon and Compensation; The Court Will Summon Guarantor Yu Qiaqing 154

Li Guojie, the former general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, mortgaged four warehouses to the China Business Corporation and entered into a ship charter agreement with the Dalai Shipping Company, damaging national sovereignty. In the civil lawsuit, Li Sihao and Yu Qiaqing posted bail on June 6th of this year, but no money has been paid. Therefore, Li did not appear yesterday, and the trial could not proceed. A General Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce Changes in July and August of This Year (Continued) (XXXVIII of the General Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce) Chinese Credit Compilation Chief Editor

The following are major changes in the shipping and hotel industries under the special industry category:

1. Yuda Shipping Company's Shanghai Branch Closes Down - The company's head office was located in Yingkou, established by Chinese merchants Bao Yucai and others. It held a significant position in the shipping industry in North China. After the fall of the Northeast, the company was once confiscated by the puppet Manchukuo authorities because it was believed to have shares held by important figures from the Northeast. Later, after efforts by local business circles, the puppet state registered its shares and sent personnel to monitor it before resuming operations. Unexpectedly, in the summer of the 1923rd year, the puppet authorities took over the company again and appointed a Japanese person as the general manager. Since then, the company's ships have been exclusively engaged in transporting Japanese goods to and from Yingkou and Japan. In recent years, smuggling has been rampant, and Yuda's ships have been used as tools for carrying contraband, flying the puppet state's flag and refusing inspection.

The Longkou Customs authorities detained it. However, the ship that was detained eventually took advantage of the Customs' unpreparedness and escaped on its own. After the Customs learned about this, in addition to issuing a general order for investigation and arrest, it also revoked the license. The Shanghai branch of the company, seeing that the ship was unable to come south again, and assuming that the remaining two ships would be the same, immediately announced its closure.

2. Paramount Hotel Closes - This hotel was a well-known large-scale hotel in Shanghai, established in the winter of the 1923rd year. It was under the jurisdiction of the Dacheng Co., Ltd., with Gu Chongqing as the chairman of the board and Zhu Hongru as the general manager. Since its opening, although it has been known for its complete equipment and outstanding reputation, the market has been sluggish and business has not improved. Most of the street-front houses have not been rented out, and the losses have been unsustainable. The company convened an emergency shareholders' meeting on July 10th. It was resolved that the board of directors would do its best to maintain the status quo under the following two major principles: first, to avoid closure as much as possible and handle liquidation or call-up procedures; second, if closure was inevitable, it should be implemented one month later. The board of directors now believes that the time has indeed come when it is absolutely necessary, and the one-month period has also passed. Therefore, it has announced the closure and is handling the aftermath.

Gleanings of Spring and Autumn (Xu Xiaoting)

It is easy to see the surface spots of things, but not the inner erosion. Only seeing the truth on the surface and not looking at the dangers inside is a common problem for people in this new era.

On the level of joy, there are sometimes jumping points of fear. In the fields of fear, there are sometimes seeds of joy. To distinguish and recognize requires a clear mind to easily respond.

Society is a kaleidoscope. The internal complexity can easily make people dizzy. It is clear that one is standing in the circle of happiness, but a misstep can lead to the abyss of fear. It is clear that one has fallen into the abyss of fear, but a jump can lead to the circle of happiness. The subtle mysteries are difficult for ordinary young people to understand.

We know to avoid polluted air, we know to improve unclean drinks, but we do not know to escape dangerous roads in society. This is the harm of recognizing the surface but not the inner layers. It is like biting into a hollow pear. From the sweet flesh, we must guard against the terrible worms wriggling in the core.

Remembering the National Hero Lü Xiaochun (Qiulang)

Mr. Lü Liuliang of Yuxi (ie Chongde), styled Wancun, was born at the end of the Ming Dynasty. He had great ambitions and was well-versed in literature, writing extensively. Because he lamented the collapse of the Ming society and the Han people falling under foreign rule, he established theories and wrote articles to advocate revolution, eagerly thinking of reviving the Han cause. Because of this, he offended the Qing court, causing literary persecution that led to his coffin being opened and his corpse mutilated, and implicated his relatives. Alas, the fate of national heroes is truly tragic and cruel!

The other day, while drinking at Qi's house, a certain gentleman from Xixiang told me in great detail about Mr. Lü's anecdotes. At a time when the country is facing internal troubles and daily increasing foreign threats, I am even more inclined to cherish this national hero! Mr. Lü's morality and writing were highly regarded by the literary circles at the time. Therefore, many famous officials, scholars, and patriots came to pay their respects. But in his actions and movements, Mr. Lü always hated the Manchus as enemies. When going out, regardless of the weather, he always wore wooden thick-soled clogs and carried an umbrella on his shoulder. His intention was probably not to share the same sky with the foreign race. Mr. Lü had one wife and one concubine, and several children. The strangest thing was that once, when he was near death, he summoned his children to his front and earnestly instructed them that on his remains, they should make another long board on which the four characters "Seeing the Sun Again" should be written, and he instructed that it should be buried in the rightmost hole in the grave (according to secular burial custom, Mr. Lü should be in the middle, the wife on the left, and the concubine on the right). Otherwise, it would be a great act of filial impiety. By the time the Qing court made its final judgment, Mr. Lü, his wife, and his concubine had all passed away. Because of the strict order to investigate and destroy all books, the officials were ordered to exhume the corpse! And all relatives were imprisoned and punished. However, the official sent was also Mr. Lü's student, but fearing the power of the Qing court, he did not dare to disobey the order. Therefore, in the dark of night, he secretly offered sacrifices and secretly ordered the relatives to flee outside, and bribed the workers to dig up the concubine's hole on the right to cover up the matter. Unexpectedly, when the coffin lid was opened, "Seeing the Sun Again" was visible, and Mr. Lü's remains were exposed! They were shocked! Could it be that Mr. Lü had foresight? Or was it preordained?

The Old Horse-Cart Driver (Zhou Xian)

I saw a statistic from Shanghai recently that claimed there were only seventeen horse-drawn carriages left in Shanghai. It's hard to imagine that the horse-drawn carriage, which once held the position of today's automobile and had its moment of glory, has declined to such an extent that it is gradually becoming qualified to be included in a museum. Mentioning this really can't help but make people feel the changes of time.

The landlord of the house I live in now was a horse-cart driver twenty years ago. The general impression is that a horse-cart driver is someone who wears a crooked hunting cap and tied-leg pants, and on top of that, a vest, someone of a vulgar demeanor. But my landlord is not such a person. He is now wearing the same long gown and mandarin jacket, his actions are very refined, and his speech is quite unconventional because he has given up the life of pulling reins for twenty years. He is now a small landlord in Shanghai, owning a self-built seven-up and seven-down house.

Although he is now a small capitalist over sixty years old, and his two sons both have very noble professions, he does not shy away from his humble origins. He himself said that he had lived a life of pulling reins for fifteen years. At that time, he had also served in a very wealthy mansion in Shanghai. There were a total of four horse-drawn carriages in that mansion, and he pulled the one that the master sat in. On average, the master only lived in Shanghai for more than two months a year.

Finally, he served in the house of a British taipan. The British taipan, seeing that he was very honest and diligent, changed his position to "houseboy" in the third year of pulling the reins for him, and sent his two sons to school to study. After serving in the British household for eleven years, one son entered the customs and the other entered the post office, so he retired. After retirement, he received a pension from the taipan, plus more than twenty years of savings, so he bought land and built a seven-up and seven-down house. Now he spends his days enjoying his old age with his grandchildren.

This old landlord lives very frugally. His daughters-in-law live with him and dare not be extravagant. Because if the daughters-in-law occasionally indulge in luxury, he would often scold them loudly, saying, "Don't you know what's good for you? You are living this kind of life now because I pulled it out with reins."

Switching the Phoenix (Written by Zhang Henshui)

Chapter Eight: Pledging Hearts with a Cup of Water in a Weary Conversation under the Green Lamp; Expressing Yearning with Embroidered Finger and Red Beans

Menglan then stood up, poured most of a cup of cold tea from the pot on the table, and drank it all in one gulp. As Chang poured the tea, the water from the spout rushed into the cup with a soft sound. Youmei intertwined her hands, placed them in her arms, sat sideways, and only looked at the white circle on the table illuminated by the lamp, not making a sound. After Menglan finished drinking the tea, she stood up, walked forward, grasped Menglan's hands with both hands, and said very calmly: "According to what you say, you don't get comfort, you get pain. Why do you do this?" Menglan said: "Naturally, there is no comfort. But I don't feel any pain. Because I was originally in pain." Youmei said: "Does he understand your background very well?" Menglan said: "So far, my exchanges with him are only in writing. And the words that come and go, in the hands of a cautious person like me, cannot be very explicit, which is imaginable. You probably know his character better than I do. Since my letters are very polite and empty, of course, his letters cannot be substantial." Youmei said: "Does he give you many letters?" Menglan said: "How can there be many? I used to be very afraid that the letters would fall into the hands of others and cause trouble. So my brother stood up and he was willing to forward the letters. Although this is a very frank action on my brother's part, I myself feel a little ashamed." Youmei said: "Okay, now there is me, who can speak on both sides. In the future, if you have letters, just give them to me. Rain or shine, I will personally deliver them to his hands. At the same time, if he has letters for you, I will also deliver them to your hands. If there is no time to write letters, I can also report oral messages to both sides. In this way, the exchange of letters will be much safer. Do you trust me?" Menglan said: "Unless I myself am ashamed and inconvenient to bother my friends with this matter, how can I say I don't trust you?" Youmei shook his hand, looked at his face, and saw that his face was deeply flushed with two red blushes, and the range was very large, even the roots of his ears were red. The evening was cool, but his body was sweating hot. Yin Dao said: "Lan, you are too excited today when you speak, and you are sweating all over. Let's talk about it another day. We can rest." Menglan said: "Am I excited? But I feel that there are many things I want to say that I haven't said yet. But don't suspect that I still have something to hide from you, but I just feel that there are thousands of things in my mind, and I don't know which sentence to say." (98)

Written by the side of three copper plates of roasted sweet potatoes (Sorrow)

Things in Shanghai are really expensive to death. Three copper plates only bought two small roasted sweet potatoes that were "rice-sized."

This is precisely the season when sweet potatoes are ripe, and it is from the beautiful hometown that one runs to this ugly, ugly Shanghai.

Sweet potatoes, this thing, are something that the tycoons, dignitaries, young masters, and young ladies of Shanghai Beach do not have the fortune to eat. Maybe they will think that it is food for pigs. However, it (sweet potato) is not like that in the countryside along the Sheyang Lake and the Yellow River. Every "farm household" treats it as their life. Without it, eating grain for a winter and a spring becomes a problem.

Man, Xin, Bo, and I all love to eat sweet potatoes. Every time the sweet potatoes are ripe, we spend all day in the sweet potato fields.

Now, Man has been lured by vanity and has become the concubine of a low-ranking bureaucrat! Xin has also become the young lady of a "embroidered pillow" young master. Since Bo entered ×× school, she has also been infected with the habits of extravagance and lost her innocence. I have also been squeezed by life and have drifted to Shanghai.

The sweet potato fields in my hometown are still the same, but we who love to eat sweet potatoes have all completely changed!

Three Great Inventions of 1936 (A Wren's Guest)

The rustling wind in the lush trees laments their swaying and falling, the cold light washes the distant sky, who can pull back the setting sun's spear, mixed with thousands of sorrows?

The above introduction commemorates Hu Maoyi, who died in the United States on October 14th, eighteen years ago.

The fierce energy of the nine heavens wildly fills the world, not leaving a pool to extinguish the "sunspots", one torch eventually becomes the blaze of the European war, fish in the pond suffer the fire's ravages throughout the world.

The above sings of sunspots. It is said: After a great war, there must be a great plague. The Paris Morning Post recently published a strange article, saying: Sunspots are volcanic holes on the sun's surface, and their power extends far to the Earth. In years of particularly large sunspots, they cause world wars and plagues.

Two malignant spirits rise, myriad horses gallop together, petty people rise, poisonous seedlings grow, beyond the Atlantic, in a sunken, gloomy land, every year we must not forget this sunny day.

The above sings of two malignant spirits. It says: The medium for the spread of the Spanish flu is one, bacteria visible to the naked eye, and two, poisonous seedlings invisible under a microscope. The two are indispensable. If cold, gloomy air accumulates on the ground without hot and cold exchange, then the two will surely rage wildly, galloping like horses, unstoppable. This is an astonishing new theory of inventors. I have heard that famous figures in the medical field of Western civilized countries are fighting the flu with all their strength, as if facing a formidable enemy, like those preventing tuberculosis and cancer. How can we not pay attention to the various descriptions of the flu because of Maoyi's death.

My life has limits, but "thought" is endless, a thousand trillion years, only a mound of earth, waiting to scoop water from the Milky Way, to offer chrysanthemum and maple leaves at the clear altar.

The above sings of the age of the Earth. According to the report of British experts examining rocks in the Great Solid State of the United States and other places, the Earth has existed for two thousand trillion years since its creation, which is also an astonishing statement. Using it in poetry is truly a new and original idea.

Brief Biographies - Anecdotes of World Tennis Giant Tilden (Zhi Zhi)

World professional tennis giant Tilden and Vines are currently touring the Far East. They first visited Japan, performing six matches for a reward of 100,000 yuan. They arrived in Shanghai on the 5th of this month and performed on the 6th. Although the weather was overcast and rainy, there were still more than 3,000 spectators, and the ticket revenue reached more than 10,000 yuan. They left Shanghai on the evening of the 6th for Hong Kong and Manila. On the 20th of this month, they will return to Shanghai for another performance before returning to the United States. In mid-December, they will rush back to the United States for MGM Pictures to produce five tennis films. These two giants in the world of tennis are unfolding the great skills of the highest level of world tennis technology before our eyes. It cannot be said that this is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity.

Tilden's original name is William T. "Big Bill" Tilden 2nd. He was born in Germantown, Pa. in the United States on February 10, 1893. He is now forty-three years old. He has dedicated his life to tennis. He started learning at the age of six, and won the children's group championship at the age of seven. When he was studying at the University of Pennsylvania at the age of eighteen, he was already one of the world-famous players. He graduated from university in 1922. Since 1920, he has quickly won the US Open tennis championship for seven years, represented the United States in the Davis Cup for eleven years, and was ranked first in the world tennis rankings for ten years. In 1920, 1922, and 1930, he won the Wimbledon Championship. The last time he won, he was thirty-eight years old. In the same year, he left amateur life and joined the professional tennis world.

Tilden's success in life is entirely due to his perseverance, constant research, calm judgment during battles, courage, and wisdom, all of which are essential to his success. In the 1922s, a poisonous sore suddenly grew on his right middle finger, and the upper half of his middle finger was finally cut off. He thought he would have to give up his tennis life from now on, but he continued to work hard and it did not affect his skills. Because of his subsequent efforts, he became the number one tennis player in the world.

Because he is committed to the tennis industry, he has forged an indissoluble bond with tennis throughout his life. He has not married yet, nor does he want to marry. In the prosperous and confusing environment of New York, he is not stained by the mud. Women and wine cannot get close to him. He only occasionally smokes cigarettes, but he does not smoke within a few hours before and after the game. In addition to concentrating on court strategy, he is also a writer. His writing is very fluent. He has written more than a dozen tennis books, all of which are very wonderful and popular all over the world. There are translations in various countries, which will be passed down forever and benefit young people who come later. His contribution is not insignificant. Although he is a great championship player, he is also very interested in drama. Because of his naive nature, he is a famous stage clown. At the same time, he can also write scripts and has served as a stage supervisor. Undoubtedly, he is also a playwright. When performing tennis, he often tries his best to display his humorous and funny clown art to entertain the audience.

His personality is straightforward and unyielding. He does not like to flatter people. If the referee makes a mistake during the game, regardless of which side the error affects, he will immediately correct it. He is the same when criticizing a tennis player. He also said that the British tennis player Pan Lai, who has won the world championship for three consecutive years (Pan also formally joined the professional tennis world by receiving Tilden's professional tennis company contract in the middle of this month), does not have very good skills. Pan Lai did not succeed, so he said. Now that Pan Lai has succeeded, he still says so and will never change his consistent position. But for Kramm of Germany, he has always praised him.

An Appeal for the Health of Children in Rural Township Elementary Schools Across the Country (Part 1) by Xie Yuheng

I. Current Rural Township Health and Rural Township Elementary School Children

China's recent rural revitalization movement can be considered a vigorous upsurge that once flourished. Rural township health facilities emerged in response. However, due to the failure to recognize a far-reaching, enduring, universal, and fundamental significance in the mission of the rural revitalization movement, the development of rural health has been wavering in the midst of thunder, wind, and rain. Generally, hygiene work in the rural movement can be categorized into two types. One is relief-oriented, where hygiene work is mixed with charitable endeavors, merely involving diagnosis and medication, completely losing the essence of rural hygiene. The other is demonstrative, where hygiene work is relatively comprehensive but still carries the color of the former. Although China lost the four northeastern provinces, the number of rural areas remaining is still substantial. If hygiene work remains relief-oriented or demonstrative, it lacks universality and long-term significance.

According to the "Survey Table of General Conditions of Rural Health in China" in Li's book "Problems of Rural Health in China," in such a vast country, only seventeen places are running rural health programs: one established by the central government, two by counties or cities, eight jointly by counties/cities and the central government or private organizations, and six by private organizations or schools. The total number of staff is only one hundred and eighty-seven. The current state of rural health can be seen from this. Among these, only a few places such as the Plain Teaching Society Experimental Zone in Ding County delve into rural areas to handle rural health and care for the health of rural township elementary school children. Although county hospitals are listed within the rural scope, their work is limited to the county's urban area. How many of the farmers who toil year-round, living in hardship and poverty, benefit from them? How much protection do the health of elementary school children in townships receive? The relationship between China's rural township health and the health of rural township elementary school children is clear today!

II. The Unhealthy Condition of Rural Township Elementary School Students

Since the First Health Office in Beiping advocated for school health in 1925, cities that are more prosperous have intermittently established school health programs. However, the number is still limited. In 1934, the Department of Health collected statistics on physical examinations from various places. Those with defects accounted for more than 95%, including 10% suffering from malnutrition, 30% from skin diseases, 50% from eye diseases, 40% from dental diseases, and 25% from tonsil diseases. In addition, the number of those suffering from other diseases was also considerable. The Department of Health also collaborated with the Ministry of Education to examine the physical condition of over 20,000 students in specialized fields and above, among whom more than 7,000 had diseases, with one-third suffering from chronic infectious diseases. From these two statistics, it is evident that the physical condition of students in China is so unsound that it undoubtedly affects the health of the entire nation! Students in cities have a better life, and the environment provides a lot of health benefits due to material civilization, yet their physical condition is still so unsound. Moreover, the family circumstances of students in specialized fields and above are much better than the average person, yet their physical condition is also unhealthy.

Imagine the extent to which the physical condition of rural children, living in the four major ailments of poverty, ignorance, disease, and selfishness, must be compromised. If there are a few experts who genuinely care about the health of rural children, or a local administrative official, who can personally and practically take a trip to the countryside (the county seat is not the countryside), they can see many children with sores, eye problems, limping feet, mumps, festering hands and feet, ringworm, runny noses, pockmarked faces, bone tuberculosis, and other diseases. If defects are examined, there could be 100% statistical deviation. No one guarantees their health, and no one treats their diseases. Compared to children in cities, the difference is as vast as heaven and earth. At that time, there would be no need to appeal for their health problems. Experts or administrative officials would surely feel pity. Children in rural townships are ardently hoping that experts and administrative officials will take measures to protect their health out of compassion.

III. The Importance of Rural Township Children's Health

China is an agricultural country, with rural land accounting for over 95% and farmers accounting for over 85%. The foundation of the country, the strength of the country, and the economy of the country are entirely built on the entire rural area. At a time when national difficulties are severe and crises are lurking, the movement to revitalize rural areas is an urgent need. No matter how serious the national difficulties are, we must consistently obey the government's response policies externally and work harder on rural construction internally, diagnose and treat the poverty, ignorance, weakness, and selfishness in rural areas, and prepare to support the country in times of crisis. Mr. Yan Yangchu said in the mission of the rural movement: "Today, the main goal of the rural movement should especially focus on rural youths. These youths can not only be good successors but also excellent future workers. They can also be a fresh force to save China and a vanguard to transform China. Taking Ding County as an example, out of the 400,000 people in the county, 80,000 are young farmers. Considering China's 400 million people, the number of rural youths in China should be at least 80 million. In the past, Xiang Yu destroyed the Qin and revived the Chu with only 8,000 soldiers. If China concentrates its efforts to transform these 80 million young farmers, I believe no national difficulty can stand up to us, and no national humiliation cannot be wiped away. Only then will all construction have a stable foundation and a solid base." Today's rural youth are so important. If we want a strong country, then we should actively provide good education to the future young farmers—rural township children—so that they can continue to work hard on national construction and revive China's authority. Therefore, today's children in rural townships have the responsibility to catch up quickly and continue to strive for China's rejuvenation, which is not only something that urban children can accomplish in the future. In today's China, how many places are working hard on this? The current young farmers have not been able to be transformed, and the future young farmers have not been given appropriate education. If this continues, who will we rely on for rural revitalization, national construction, coping with national crises, and supporting the country in times of crisis? Now, in addition to actively transforming young farmers, we must also provide good education to future young farmers. Furthermore, historically, many heroes and great men who have achieved great success have been "country folks" who came from the fields. From these two points, we can see the importance of educating children in rural townships, especially given the current poor physical condition and prevalence of diseases among rural children. Currently, in terms of education for rural children, although there is free education, it is still not widespread. Who is paying attention to their well-being? If there are knowledgeable farmers but no healthy farmers, how can the country be strong? The importance of the health of children in rural townships is undeniable.

An Overview of the Work of the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association in the Past Three Years and Future Plans by Yan Fuqing 156

This association was initiated by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, who connected leaders from various Chinese and foreign circles and giants in the medical field. The inaugural meeting was held on October 21, 1933, at the Municipal Government Reception Office on Avenue Joffre. Wu Tiecheng was elected as honorary president, Niu Huisheng as chairman, Li Ting'an as vice-chairman, and Yan Fuqing, Weng Zhilong, and Bu Mei as executive directors. In 1934, Niu Huisheng requested leave due to illness, and the position of chairman was temporarily filled by Vice-Chairman Li Ting'an according to the law. In 1935, Chairman Niu Huisheng repeatedly requested resignation, which was approved at the fifth executive director meeting in mid-September of that year. Lu Bohong was elected as chairman. In October 1936, when the annual meeting was held, directors and supervisors were re-elected in accordance with the regulations. As a result, Wu Tiecheng, Lu Bohong, Li Ting'an, Yan Fuqing, Huang Zifang, Weng Zhilong, Qiao Deng, Shi Siming, Chen Heqin, Pan Gongzhan, Gan Xiaoying, and other eleven people were elected as executive directors. Du Yuesheng, Pang Jingzhou, Ding Fubao, Qian Xinzhi, Yao Mulian, Yu Qiaqing, Liu Zhanen, and other seven people were regularly elected as supervisors. The overview of the work in the past three years is described as follows:

(1) Soliciting Members—Anti-tuberculosis work cannot be done by the efforts of one or two individuals or one or two organizations alone. It requires the joint participation of people from all walks of life to be effective. Therefore, after its establishment, the association immediately solicited members and raised funds to strengthen its power. Subsequently, it held a fundraising conference every year. The first fundraising conference was opened on December 15, 1934, at the Banking Association on Hong Kong Road, raising 300 members and donations of more than 18,000 yuan. The opening ceremony of the second fundraising conference was held on April 6, 1935, at Mayor Wu's residence, raising 800 members and donations of more than 7,300 yuan. The third fundraising conference was held at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA on April 18 of this year. From the date of establishment to June 25 of this year, a total of 35,828.39 yuan was collected in membership fees, donations, X-ray fees, and bank interest.

(2) Publicity—At the beginning of its establishment, in addition to striving to carry out various practical tasks, the association also paid attention to publicity matters to awaken the nation's attention to the anti-tuberculosis movement and instill preventive methods and treatment knowledge. Publicity matters can be divided into two aspects:

(1) Oral Publicity—(1) Holding popular lectures at various schools, organizations, and public places, totaling 40 sessions and reaching 25,000 people. (2) Radio Lectures—Broadcasting lectures on various radio stations, totaling 20 sessions. (3) Conducting a campaign to discourage spitting—One session each last year and this year, with 14 lectures and 7,000 listeners, and distributing 15,000 copies of special publications and leaflets on the campaign to discourage spitting.

(2) Written Publicity: (1) Publishing anti-tuberculosis monthly magazines and health pictorials (bi-weekly), which are edited and issued by the association on a regular basis, with a total distribution of more than 100,000 copies. (2) Posting various slogans—Mobile advertisements on streetcars and buses, as well as wall advertisements in important places on the road, totaling 15,000 copies. (3) Holding anti-tuberculosis exhibitions—In January 1935, an anti-tuberculosis exhibition was held at the YMCA on Sichuan Road, lasting for three days and attracting more than 3,000 visitors. (4) Compiling anti-tuberculosis health posters—A total of 40 types, each printed in 1,000 copies, distributed to various schools, organizations, and institutions for posting. (5) Donating anti-tuberculosis books—"Guide to Lung Disease," "Prevention of Lung Disease," and "Treatment of Lung Disease," totaling more than 3,000 copies. (6) Composing five types of anti-tuberculosis songs—Distributed to various schools, organizations, and singing groups, totaling 3,500 copies.

(3) Establishing Clinics—In order to meet social needs and prevent the spread of tuberculosis, the association established the First Clinic on West Lin Road, West Gate, on June 14, 1934. On April 1, 1935, the Second Clinic was added on Duojia Road, South City. On January 7, 1936, the Third Clinic was added on Tibet Road. However, the Second and Third Clinics have been relocated due to contractual issues with the location. The Second Clinic is now located in the Qingyun Road Health Office. The Third Clinic has been temporarily suspended due to a shortage of manpower. All clinics provide free medical treatment to patients. Since the establishment of the clinics, more than 5,000 citizens have visited for treatment, which proves the prevalence of tuberculosis among the citizens.

In addition, there are home visits. Nurses from the clinics visit patients' homes every morning to inform them of various methods of prevention and treatment, so that patients can learn how to maintain their health and avoid infecting their families.

In addition to treating tuberculosis patients, the association's clinics also

Page 16

conduct tuberculin tests for elementary school students, totaling 385 children. The results are as follows:

In addition, National Jiaotong University, Shanghai Business School, and Shanghai University have entrusted the association's clinics to use X-ray machines to fluoroscope the lungs of new students to conduct physical examinations upon admission. The anti-tuberculosis work has attracted the attention of various schools, which is deeply gratifying. In total, more than 300 new university students have had their lungs examined by X-ray.

(4) Holding Summer Children's Health Camps—In June 1934, the association co-sponsored the first Shanghai Summer Children's Health Camp with the Municipal Education Bureau, Health Bureau, Children's Welfare Association, Chenbao Newspaper, and other organizations. The camp was held at Tongji Middle School in Wusong, with a total of 60 boys and girls enrolled, with good results. In June 1935, the second Summer Children's Health Camp was held, with the number of children enrolled reaching 180. In June of this year, the third Summer Children's Health Camp was held, with more than 20 participating groups and the number of children enrolled soaring to 220, which is an important endeavor to promote outdoor activities for children.

(5) Publishing Anti-Tuberculosis Magazines—In order to popularize anti-tuberculosis education, after several preparations, the anti-tuberculosis monthly magazine was launched in November 1934. Since its publication, it has been well-received by all sectors of society. In June of this year, it was changed to Health Pictorial (bi-weekly). The education sector in various places is very interested in the publication, considering it a good supplementary reading material for health education.

(6) Conducting a Campaign to Discourage Spitting—Spitting everywhere easily spreads tuberculosis bacteria, no different from setting up a machine gun on the road. The Chinese people are deeply rooted in this bad habit, and it is impossible to eradicate it with just a few days of publicity. Therefore, the association decided to hold large-scale publicity once every March and April to awaken the nation and eradicate the bad habit of spitting everywhere. The publicity in the past two years has attracted the attention of the general public! It is gratifying.

(7) Participating in Health Campaigns—The association has participated in the annual Shanghai Municipal Health Campaign since its establishment, taking on the anti-tuberculosis movement in the conference. In addition to expanding publicity to make the public aware of the severity of tuberculosis and the methods of prevention and treatment, each session also sends letters to various hospitals and doctors to provide free physical examinations and half-price X-rays for soldiers. In addition, it participated in the Zhenjiang Health Education Exhibition this year and received a certificate of merit.

(8) Holding Anti-Tuberculosis Exhibitions—We recognize that tuberculosis has many types and complex symptoms, making it difficult for the general public to understand and prevent. Therefore, on October 3, 1935, we held an anti-tuberculosis exhibition at the Sichuan Road YMCA. With the assistance of municipal organizations and medical groups, it went very smoothly. The exhibits included tuberculosis models, charts, statistical cartoons, slogans, and more than 1,000 items. It is estimated that 500 to 600 people attended that day. The audience was able to generally understand the types of tuberculosis, the symptoms of each stage, and the methods of prevention and treatment, leaving a deep impression. (To be continued)

Common Sense Questions and Answers about Diseases by Cheng Hanzhang 157

(97) Lymphatic Constitution and Exudative Diathesis

(Question) What is called a lymphatic constitution?

(Answer) This is a type of abnormal constitution. Children often have chronic swelling of the lymph nodes, and their skin and mucous membranes are prone to pathological changes. Later, they are also prone to bone and joint lesions, which is called a child with a lymphatic constitution.

(Question) How is the word "constitution" explained?

(Answer) This is a commonly used term, which refers to the inherent strength of the human body to suffer from certain types of diseases. In a broad sense, diabetes, obesity, bronchial asthma, hemophilia, neuralgia, etc., can all be attributed to abnormal constitutions.

(Question) What does a person with a lymphatic constitution look like?

(Answer) They are mostly pale, with withered skin, relaxed muscles, and a swollen face, and thick and protruding lips; this is called a sluggish lymphatic constitution. There are also those with flushed skin and veins visible under the skin, which is called a sensitive lymphatic constitution.

(Question) Do people with a lymphatic constitution have changes in the lymph nodes?

(Answer) Yes. People with this constitution have painless swelling of the lymph nodes in the neck, mandible angle, and nape of the neck (commonly known as phlegm nodes).

(Question) What are the changes in the skin?

(Answer) Children with this constitution are most prone to eczema, lupus, or pruritic lichen, etc.

(Question) What are the changes in the mucous membranes?

(Answer) The mucous membranes of the conjunctiva, cornea, nasal passages, and middle ear often develop inflammation.

(Question) What are the changes in the bones and joints?

(Answer) The changes in the bones and joints are the development of tuberculous osteitis and periostitis, or white swelling, bone ulcers, etc. later.

(Question) What is the cause of lymphatic constitution after all?

(Answer) Children born to parents with tuberculosis are mostly of a lymphatic constitution. Children with congenital syphilis also exhibit the same lymphatic constitution.

(Question) What is called an exudative diathesis?

(Answer) This is different from lymphatic constitution and has nothing to do with tuberculosis or syphilis. Those who are born with a diathesis where the skin and mucous membranes often develop diseases are specifically called exudative diathesis.

(Question) What are the diseases of the skin and mucous membranes suffered by people with exudative diathesis?

(Answer) People with this constitution often suffer from urticaria, eczema, pyoderma, and swollen lymphatic nodes, adenoid hyperplasia, etc. The mucous membranes are also prone to inflammation, such as colds, rhinitis, stomatitis, conjunctivitis, otitis media, otorrhea, etc.

(Question) What should be the treatment for lymphatic constitution and exudative diathesis?

(Answer) The first thing in the treatment of lymphatic constitution and exudative diathesis is to pay attention to diet and hygiene; second, to take cod liver oil regularly; third, to carry out opposite therapy; fourth, to take salt spring baths every day; fifth, to carry out artificial sun lamp and sunlight irradiation therapy.

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued) by Zhou Mengbai 158

Verbenaceae

I. Vitex cannabifolia, Sieb. et Zucc, (V. Negundo, L.)

"Plant" Originally produced in China, it is a self-growing deciduous shrub. The leaves are opposite, with long stalks, palmately compound, with leaflets, each leaflet is lanceolate or long oval, with coarsely serrated edges and acuminate tips. Terminal panicles, blooming pale purple small labiate flowers in summer. The drupe is spherical, black when ripe.

Large Vitex heterophylla, Roxb. is a tree, and its leaves are larger than the previous species. The flowers are pale yellowish-white.

"Crude Drug" Vitex Fruitus Cannabifoliae is collected from its fruits. This product is spherical, with a diameter of only six millimeters, and the surface is dark brown.

Vitex Succus is made by cutting its roots to a length of 30 cm, baking them greatly, and collecting the juice exuding from both ends.

"Medicinal Use" Old sayings: Vitex fruit is effective for colds and is used as a decoction. Vitex Succus is an expectorant. The daily dose is 4-12 cm.

II. Vitex trifolia, L. var. Ovata, Makino

"Plant" It mostly grows on sandy beaches by the sea and is a deciduous small shrub. The trunk is recumbent. The leaves have stalks, are oval, entire, round-headed, and densely covered with white hair on the reverse side. Terminal cymes, blooming small purple labiate flowers in summer. The drupe is spherical.

"Crude Drug" Vitex trifoliae Fruitus, which is harvested from its fruits and dried. This product is spherical, with a diameter of about five millimeters. The pericarp is dark black, hard, and not easy to break, and is partly covered with thin persistent sepals. The cross-section has four rooms. The taste is slightly harsh and has a peculiar aroma.

"Ingredients" It has not been found out whether the fruit contains essential oil. The leaves contain 0.28% essential oil, and the small branches contain 0.11% essential oil. The main components of this oil are Campben (55%) Dipentenalkobol (20%) Terpinylacetat (3-19%) Pinen, etc.

"Medicinal Use" Old sayings: Vitex trifoliae is a tonic and cooling medicine, and it is also used to treat headaches, colds, etc. It is also used as a bath soup material by the people.

III. Verbena officinalis, L. Eisenkraut (German) Peristerion (English)

(Plant) It grows naturally in warm areas of Japan and is a perennial herb. The stem is up to one meter high. The whole plant has pilose hair. The leaves are opposite, obovate or long oval, lobed or pinnately deeply divided. Terminal spicate inflorescences, blooming pale purple shallowly lobed funnel-shaped small flowers in summer.

(Crude Drug) Verbenae Herba, which is collected from its whole grass and dried.

(Ingredients) The whole grass contains Vnrbenalin C17H25O10 (crystalline glycoside).

(Medicinal Use) In Japan, Verbena is squeezed into juice or decocted for application to tumors and various skin diseases, and it is also used as a washing material.

Explanation of Blood Transfusion (Continued) by Jiang Yisheng 159

(IV) How good the rules are, the results depend entirely on human actions—Now, please discuss lawyers and doctors together for easy understanding. Lawyers use knowledge and skills to protect human rights within the scope of the law, and doctors use knowledge and skills to protect human lives within the scope of the law. Therefore, the two are regarded as liberal professions, are valued by society, and have legal protection for their powers. Lawyers deal with cases, and human and material evidence sometimes requires detailed scientific examination and citation. Not only must every word be based on evidence and be reasonable, but it must also comply with the law. Doctors treat diseases, and observation, auscultation, questioning, and palpation are superficial matters. Not only must there be subjective judgment, but also objective examinations to prove without doubt before diagnosis and treatment. This is scientific medicine, which is in line with the scientific rules. Those who manipulate words and use eloquent tongues to reverse black and white, distorting the truth for self-interest, are called tricksters and are not lawyers. Those who make alarming statements, talk nonsense, deceive the world, do not follow the law, do not abide by the standards of science, and only know self-interest without prioritizing the interests of patients are called quacks and are not doctors.

Returning to the topic, in short, blood transfusion is performed to save lives. A corresponding surgery fee is charged, and the blood recipient gives the blood donor a reward, without taking any commission. When the extremely poor need blood transfusion, they also try their best to arrange it. Voluntary blood donors are prepared in advance, and hospital nurses and workers nearby are selected to serve. Such doctors are the same as fair and wise lawyers who are willing to speak up for justice. Those who perform surgery for the sake of surgery fees, regardless of whether the patient needs it or not, and those who transfuse blood for the sake of blood transfusion rewards are no different from pimps who buy rural women for financial exploitation. If there is such a person and if there are co-authors, I will write to condemn him and file a lawsuit to sue him. I will gladly hold the whip for them. However, I will never agree with the argument of giving up eating because of choking.

In response, Yu Ran Shen Tong firmly and loudly shouted, "We should cherish blood and not kill it invisibly, nor sacrifice it meaninglessly. We should not value blood, but see how it is used! The great rivers and mountains are filled with smoke and miasma. If we don't use our blood, how can we wash it clean?! How can the nation prosper?! The principle is the same as the blood transfusion law." (The End)

"Are the Words of a Dying Man Good?" by Yin Fei 163

"The words of a dying man are good." This is an old saying. According to Chinese custom, anything that is qualified to be called "old" becomes an iron law that cannot be denied. Usually, probably because of fear of being a traitor, it seems that few people dare to say a "no" to this iron law.

But are the words of a dying man really "good"? I think it's not necessarily true, at least it's not necessarily all good.

When a prisoner is about to be executed, there is always a pastor to pray for him, asking God to elevate him, but there is also a condition attached, that is, the prisoner must confess his sins during his lifetime. It seems that after such a confession, the sinful soul immediately becomes holy and can go to heaven.

In such a situation, the stubborn prisoner is stubborn to the end, not only refusing to confess, but also shouting "In twenty years, I will be a good man again!" Because of this, it is common for pastors to be at a loss. Such prisoners are generally given an epithet by those who are responsible for teaching and persuading them, saying: "He does not wake up until death." Whether he "does not wake up until death" is not to be discussed here for the time being, but it is more than enough to prove that "the words of a dying man" are not necessarily all "good."

There are not many prisoners who "do not wake up until death"; most prisoners turn pale or even sob when they hear the news of their execution. At this time, the religious force takes the opportunity to enter, and naturally becomes a painkiller for those waiting to be slaughtered. Naturally, he will do it without error; but is this the "good" of "dying"? I'm afraid it's not necessarily true. To put it bluntly, most of them think that they have committed a "crime." In this way, they can get rid of some "crime," so that they can suffer less "torture" when they arrive at "hell." It's good that this is just a matter of lifting a hand, so why not do it. Therefore, the motivation is still to get rid of sin, not to do good. As for the pastors, even they themselves do not know whether they will go to heaven after confession, but it is naturally more willing to let living people say a word of mercy and absorb some followers, which is good for him.

"Warped" prisoners "their words are not good" are originally incomprehensible, but are those who are not "warped" "good"? It's not necessarily!

Those who can "die in their sleep" and are not dying of a sudden illness usually have some "last words" when they are "dying." For ordinary people, it is always about owing debts to others and raising the old and caring for the young; as for celebrities or prominent officials, it is naturally different. In addition to how to dispose of the estate, they must add a few clauses such as "do not do this" and "do not do that" to show that even when they are sick, they have not forgotten national affairs and morality.

It may be a fact that they still remember national affairs while lying in bed, but concern is not necessarily "good." To put it absolutely, it can sometimes even be "evil": If you want to be a marquis who steals the country, you must not be indifferent to national affairs, this is one thing; second, even if you want to do good wholeheartedly, but because of the limitations of his environment and the spirit of the times, the result is that he regards arsenic as a good medicine to save the world, so he poisons people and still rejoices in his concern for the world and national affairs.

Therefore, even if his motivation is good, "his words" may not necessarily be "good." As for whether the motivation is pure, there are many places that are also beyond doubt. To put it bluntly, celebrities and prominent officials are weakened by illness and have neurasthenia. Because they have killed too many people when they are on stage, the fear of crime is sometimes even greater than that of prisoners: those who say "do not do this" and "do not do that" are sometimes a reflection of the psychology of getting rid of sin.

However, will "the words of a dying man" not have "their words are good"? Not necessarily. However, "their words are good" must be those who are usually "good" in what they "say" and do, then they will be "good in their words," but that is already different from the meaning of "the dying man."

It is impossible to do all kinds of evil in ordinary times, and then "their words are good" when "the dying man."

Window by Ziming 164

Across from the window is a dilapidated small foreign house. The ochre-red roof tiles have been weathered into a dim gray: the creeper grows as much as possible, almost sealing off a louvered window. In the cold wind of late autumn, the "for rent" wooden sign seems to be hitting the iron fence gate like a wind chime on the top of a tower.

Every day I sit at my desk reading and writing. When I hear the turbid gold sound of the for rent wooden sign hitting the iron fence post, I always stare blankly at the louvered window, wondering where the owner of this small foreign house is wandering now? Sometimes I fantasize that in the middle of the night when thunder and lightning are intertwined, the louvered window suddenly breaks the tough stems and leaves of the creeper and opens wide. A young woman with disheveled hair stands in front of the window, with two glowing eyes, flying down from the window and kneeling on the herringbone-shaped pavement, worshiping the sky and telling how she was wronged to death. Then I immediately close the window and draw the thick velvet curtains. I am afraid that I will really encounter such a female zombie.

He requested a postponement until the injured thieves recovered and the investigation was completed before filing a lawsuit for trial. Zhao confessed that he did not know about the robbery. Wang Anqing asked me to accompany him to the hospital. The court verified the confession and decided to reschedule the interrogation for 2:00 PM on the 27th. Yang Shilin, one of the four injured thieves, 43 years old, a native of Haimen, died at 2:40 PM yesterday due to a gunshot wound to a vital part of the abdomen, right next to the navel. The hospital notified the police, and the body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan sub-hall for an autopsy, and a report will be submitted to the Special First Court today to send someone to examine it.
